$$f(\epsilon, T) = 61.35\epsilon(-0.0508(T - 278.15) + 1) + 98.58\epsilon^{0.318}\exp(-49.46/(8.314T)) + 2.304\epsilon^{1.450}(T - 278.15)$$

- First term: $61.35\epsilon \cdot (-0.0508T + 0.0508 \times 278.15 + 1) = 61.35\epsilon(−0.0508T + 15.128) ≈ 61.35\epsilon(15.128 - 0.0508T)$

Wait, let me recalculate: $-0.0508 \times 278.15 + 1 = -14.128 + 1 = -13.128$... No.

$-c1*(T - c2) + c3 = -0.0508*(T - 278.15) + 1 = -0.0508T + 14.128 + 1 = -0.0508T + 15.128$

So the first term is: $61.35\epsilon(-0.0508T + 15.128)$

- Second term: $98.58\epsilon^{0.318}\exp(-5.949/T)$ (since $49.46/8.314 = 5.949$)

- Third term: $2.304\epsilon^{1.450}(T - 278.15)$

So GT has three distinct components:
1. A linear-in-$\epsilon$ term with linear $T$ dependence: $a\epsilon + b\epsilon T$
2. A fractional power of $\epsilon$ times $\exp(-k/T)$: $c\epsilon^{0.318}\exp(-d/T)$
3. A fractional power of $\epsilon$ times linear $T$: $e\epsilon^{1.450}T + f\epsilon^{1.450}$

The basis functions involved are: $\epsilon$, $\epsilon T$, $\epsilon^{0.318}\exp(-c/T)$, $\epsilon^{1.450}T$, $\epsilon^{1.450}$.

## Checking Candidate 40

$$f = (c_0 + c_1 T)\epsilon + (c_2 + c_3 T)\epsilon^{c_4}$$

This gives: $c_0\epsilon + c_1 T\epsilon + c_2\epsilon^{c_4} + c_3 T\epsilon^{c_4}$

This has basis functions: $\epsilon$, $\epsilon T$, $\epsilon^{c_4}$, $T\epsilon^{c_4}$.

The GT needs: $\epsilon$, $\epsilon T$, $\epsilon^{0.318}\exp(-c/T)$, $\epsilon^{1.450}T$, $\epsilon^{1.450}$.

The GT has $\epsilon^{1.450}$ and $\epsilon^{1.450}T$ — candidate 40 can match these with $c_4 = 1.450$. But then the $\epsilon^{0.318}\exp(-c/T)$ term cannot be represented. **No match.**

## Checking Candidate 41

$$f = c_0\epsilon^{c_1}\exp(-c_2/T)$$

Only one term — cannot match GT's multi-term structure. **No match.**

## Systematic Check

The GT requires three fundamentally different functional forms. I need a candidate with at least three terms combining: (1) $\epsilon \cdot T$ polynomial terms, (2) $\epsilon^{p}\exp(-k/T)$, and (3) $\epsilon^{q} \cdot T$ terms.

Looking through all candidates, none have all three components simultaneously. The closest candidates like #40 have polynomial-in-T times power-of-epsilon terms but lack the $\exp(-c/T)$ component. Candidates with $\exp(-c/T)$ (like #41, #8) lack the polynomial structure.

No candidate combines:
- Linear $\epsilon \cdot T$ terms
- $\epsilon^p \exp(-c/T)$ 
- $\epsilon^q \cdot T$ terms

all together in one expression.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match
